I'm PurpleLotus and the reason I am creating this thread is so that my customers, or just newbs with questions about my listings, could have a place to discuss all things PurpleLotus. First newb tip, you cannot buy the HardCore collection without owning the original collection. This is done for safety reasons and in an effoert to boost overall customer success and satisfaction. No exceptions are ever made. Learned this one the hard way through experience.

So what the hell do I sell anyway? I sell coupons which you download and can then print just like any other internet coupons and work in stores. They can be printed and used unlimited times. They are all 100% custom made, never before seen, and exclusively only sold on SilkRoad. I do expiration updates every couple of months so that they are never out of date, but also don't have a ridiculous expiration date that's way too far away. These updates are free once you have purchased my listing. I also periodically add coupons to each collection which are also free for the particular collection(s) you have purchased. For example, since the release of the Original Collection I have added over 100 new coupons which everyone who owned the collection got for free.

They work EXCELLENT at Target and K-Mart and I would say 95% of Walmart's but some remote Walmart's act fucking crazy and I think it might be a different type of scanner or something, but I always recommend to start off small at a new store that way you can learn if they are goig to be very accepting when you come back with a hand full of them. This is especially true with your local and regional chains although many of those work just fine, but it's something I can't test myself, so local and regional chains you just gotta read their coupon policy, so you make sure you don't do anything to break it from the start, and test a coupon or two to make sure you are g2g. If they dont accept it, they dont accept it... no worries, but it's embarrassing if you walk into a brand new store with 15 coupons and the store doesn't accept them, that's rare though at any store but I always recommend the small test run first.

I do in fact make custom coupons... actually my last 100+ coupons added to the OC collection were either customers suggestions or selfish PurpleLotus wants this shit too coupons. Title: Re: PurpleLotus - Vendor of USA coupons - Newbie Review Thread
Post by: purplelotus on January 18, 2013, 06:05 pm
Get a smartphone app which scans UPCs and gs1 databars, that way you can test them out for a positive scan before going out to the store. iPhone makes the best one called "coupondecoder" which will not only scan but also will break down the information contained in the coupon. Android does not have a similar app yet, but you can download barcode scanners that will atleast register the scan so you know it printed out well.

Title: Re: PurpleLotus - Vendor of USA coupons - Newbie Review Thread
Post by: Abbie Hoffman on January 18, 2013, 09:49 pm
I've used numerous OC coupons over the past couple of weeks, with rarely a hitch. I've been using the hell out of the self-checkout aisles, though I can see why a real cashier is the way to go.

The folks at Wal-Mart are so overworked and underpaid, and they're looking for idiots 'boosting' a five-fingered discount down their pants. Coupon fraud really isn't on their radar screen and you'll have no problem, as long as you look presentable and act reasonably friendly. And Target is much more customer and coupon friendly, from my experience.

The one time that a cashier balked was at a Wal-Mart, when the coupon exceeded the item price. But she didn't say a word about the nine other PL coupons, that I saved $50 on in that transaction. LOL!

I managed to get a free $15 SW GC at KMart, with a manager's approval. That's my only HC conquest... so far!

PL is great and more often proactive with customer service. The very few problems I've seen with his work, have all been fixed before I even complained about them.

For the other wussies like me who use the self-checkout lanes, do cover up the UPC and try to get the GS-1 databar to scan first. That seems to eliminate the need for at least some manager approvals.

The weekend or after 5 PM are the times to go, from what I've seen.

I've netted nearly $250 just since the first of the month (loading up on non-perishables, while the gettin's good) and I definitely owe PL a tip. Thank you, PL. Your OC collection is worth more to me than an EBT (food stamp) card!

Title: Re: PurpleLotus - Vendor of USA coupons - Newbie Review Thread
Post by: edzart on January 20, 2013, 05:14 am
On the main thread, it looks like people are discussing target returns with coupons. I'll contribute my two cents since I work there, although I dunno if this'll make it across to the other board...

yes, targets are fishy on people returning lots of items that are assumed to have been purchased with coupons. BUT here's the catch (at least at my store, which I mentioned is pretty strict)-- bullseye won't do anything about these returns. that's right, not even assets protection cares about this problem, and neither does target.

the reason for this, i've been told, is that target makes all of its money back from the manufacturers on the coupons, so they don't care and wouldn't do anything about this problem until there's a loss from it.

what target doesn't know, is that people could be returning items purchased with some purplelotus coupons.

now, usually you'll only be refunded the amount that you actually paid for the item. here's the catch though, and follow closely: pay for the items with a visa or american express gift card, using all your PL coupons too. when you want to return your items, tell them you lost the receipt, but that you paid with a gift card, asking if they can look it up on there. the less you act you know about target's policy and system for this, the more innocent you'll seem. finally, when you return the items, the entire amount (coupon value + what you paid) should be refunded to the gift card that you originally used to pay. i've seen this work for people a lot, and they weren't even using fake coupons, as far as i know. coop + gc = profits

Title: Re: PurpleLotus - Vendor of USA coupons - Newbie Review Thread
Post by: jackchurchill on January 26, 2013, 08:45 am
I just got back from a run with my brother to Walmart.  We grabbed nearly identical carts except for  a few items and split up for payment.  He went through a traditional line and I decided to try the self checkout to see if this method would be preferred in the future. We both rounded out our carts with 2 non-coupon hobby items that were $3.95 each that we intend to re-sell in bulk later to recoup cost just to make sure we were not too close to a negative balance.  My brother had perfect success with the Subway Gift Card, Tilamook cheese, Hanes Shirts, 4-pack Monster Energy Drinks, Bic Mechanical Pencils, Bounty Towel 6-Pack, 8-Pack Duracell Battery, Coffee-mate Creamer, Starbucks Coffee and the 2- $3.99 items for our non-coupon items.  He did have to speak with a CSM but we were expecting that scenario to happen eventually and it went over extremely well.  He just chatted up this middle-aged female cashier and CSM.  After some short confusion as to why the CSM was necessary, the CSM realized that it was because the savings was over $50.  Once this was realized, the CSM then made the error go away and she was on her way. 

I instantly ran into problems when my coffee creamer wouldn't scan.  The self-checkout supervisor came over and manually input the UPC after unsuccessfully trying herself a few times.  I successfully rang up the remaining groceries and then proceeded to scan my coupons.  The California Pizza and Tilamook Cheese scanned perfect as usual (probably 5 times each) and the Coffee-mate creamer also scanned perfect on my first try.  The Hanes shirts, Duracell, Bic Pens, Monster Energy, Cheez-it's and Subway Gift Card all told me to wait for assistance.  Again the supervisor came to assist me and she was unable to successfully find what the source of the problem was.  She then sought out the assistance of her immediate superior.  He came over and attempted to scan the coupons.  He tried the Subway Gift Card first and was unable to figure out why it wouldn't work.  He took the coupon with him towards the electronics section appearing to seek out his boss for help.  He came back, about 10 minutes later and tried again using another method and still failed.  He then apologized and said he could take it if it scanned properly.  While waiting for roughly ten minutes for the CSM to find his manager for guidance, I had seen my brother complete his transaction waiting from a distance.  I had sent him a text to inquire on his success and he had quickly responded on his 100% success.  Due to this knowledge, I knew I could successfully have these items scanned at a traditional register.  Once the CSM left and it was just myself and the self checkout supervisor I directed her as to which items I would be removing from this purchase and trying in a traditional line.  So my self checkout consisted of creamer, cheese and pizza which totaled out at $4.76.  The supervisor then offered to take me to her stand and finish assisting me.  My second order had Hanes, Duracell, Bic Pens, Monster Energy, Cheez-it's as well as my 2- $3.99 items.  I had accidently left the Subway card in the hands of the CSM so I missed out on trying that one but all of the other coupons worked except for the Cheez-it's which I had accidentally grabbed the wrong size but still wanted to eat Cheez-it's when stoned later.  This came out to $7.72.    Between my brother and I, we spent $20.66 with a savings of $96.93.  If I hadn't left my Subway card with the CSM, we would have saved an additional $15.  My brother and I laughed our asses off on our drive home when we realized based on sales tax, $18 of the $20.66 we had spent was on the 4- $3.99 hobby items which we intend to resell to recoup the cost (Going to make a coupon for them soon when I can afford more BTC).  We had gone there with the hopes of scoring on Visa and other gift cards and failed terribly due to the minimal inventory this particular store carried.  We had also hoped to get the HP printer which according to the Walmart site showed would likely be free but was $14 after coupon at this location so we passed.

Title: Re: PurpleLotus - Vendor of USA coupons - Newbie Review Thread
Post by: jackchurchill on January 28, 2013, 06:13 am
@ kycuong: If you look at those anti-counterfeiting websites they are a joke.  Almost all of their coupons they are posting as recently found counterfeits have already expired.  The system as it currently exists is one where it takes weeks or more for the coupons to make the trip to the clearinghouses.  The stores then have to get notified that they will not be reimbursed for the coupons and in order to really shut down a particular coupon it has to be costing the stores enough money to train their employees to spot that particular coupon and then actually care about saving their employer money.  Luckily for us, PL makes updates on coupons as people report issues and is continually adding new coupons.  Now it is even possible to make our own personalized coupons that nobody else will be using.  Both stores and manufactures have a common interest in continuing to use coupons for tax reasons as well as for marketing purposes.  They may try to improve their system but even if they overhaul their systems, someone will find a way to exploit the vulnerabilities.  You are really only trying to sneak one over on a Walmart employee.  Not exactly a daunting task.  These employees will focus more of their loss prevention in traditional theft which is easy to do and more convict-able. 

@ White 0ut: I use 7-10 on a lot of my trips but have been just scoping new places so far.  I plan to use 15-20 in the future using a combination of OC/HC and onion credit generated coupons and will be trying to keep my total cost between $10-15.  In order to convict, they have to show intent.  Enough intent that not one juror could believe any plausible excuse you gave for the coupons.  It is not your responsibility to prove innocence, it is theirs to prove guilt.  My brother and I have a great lawyer.  As the show breaking bad says "You don't want a criminal lawyer... you want a criminal lawyer."  Not really necessary for PL's coupons but if you're someone worried about the law, it can't hurt for other situations. 

Unfortunately I didn't make any trips to go shopping today since I was just recovering from a long night of mdma and drinking.  Hopefully I can get a chance to try 2-3 stores tomorrow evening and will report any new findings.

Title: Re: PurpleLotus - Vendor of USA coupons - Newbie Review Thread
Post by: jackchurchill on January 28, 2013, 07:44 am
@ White Out: Ya, it is super easy.  Any problems I have encountered were not in a manner where I was being looked at as a guilty party.  They were simply seeing if they could accept the coupon or not.  These employees are not trying to break open a 5 o'clock new story, they are simply trying not to get yelled at by their superiors for not following a the company policy which they are likely less familiar with than you should be.  Just read the coupon policy for the the store you are going to so you don't look like an idiot and get flustered and act really strange.  Although I am sure the self-checkout could be exploited very well, I have realized that with they type of savings I am looking to get, I will have to likely talk to somebody so I might as well just go to a regular cashier who will normally just take care of any issues with the OC coupons without having ever needed a manager for those.  Just be friendly and converse about something natural.  Most people hate talking about their shitty jobs, so try and find something more interesting than groceries to talk with them about and it might help you out in the long run.   

@ XyankeedoodleX: You can use cash or Visa gift Cards.  Don't use anything that traces back to you.  I do have a regional store's savings card that I filled out using fake info.  I only use the card a few times and then I can get another one for free.  The coupons are not discovered to not be authentic until they arrive at the clearinghouse that pays the stores for their coupons.  Stores such as Walmart just throw their coupons into a bin and bundle them together at the end of their shift.  You likely have a few weeks minimum before the store would have any idea a coupon didn't pay them back.  Compared to traditional theft, coupon theft is relatively low and much harder to stop, which means it costs them more money.  Most likely stores are not going to train their employees on not taking a particular coupon unless the use is so prolific that said training would in fact save them more money than the employees time costs. 

@ kycuong: Glad you liked it.  It's just important to know your rights.  Many people don't understand the rights they have, so they don't notice when they are being taken away.

@ XyankeedoodleX: You can use cash or Visa gift Cards.  Don't use anything that traces back to you.  I do have a regional store's savings card that I filled out using fake info.  I only use the card a few times and then I can get another one for free.  The coupons are not discovered to not be authentic until they arrive at the clearinghouse that pays the stores for their coupons.  Stores such as Walmart just throw their coupons into a bin and bundle them together at the end of their shift.  You likely have a few weeks minimum before the store would have any idea a coupon didn't pay them back.  Compared to traditional theft, coupon theft is relatively low and much harder to stop, which means it costs them more money.  Most likely stores are not going to train their employees on not taking a particular coupon unless the use is so prolific that said training would in fact save them more money than the employees time costs. 

Thanks for the answer! Yeah I've been thinking and the cashiers are people just like you and I. Personally if I was working at Walmart making minimum wage I wouldn't give two shits about people using fake coupons or not.

Alright so I went on a nice little trip with the coupons with my roommate today. I started out at Walmart just to grab a few things and to try out a giftcard coupon at self checkout. I went up with a $10 Burger King card and as soon as I scanned it, assistance was needed to activate the card. I also showed the self checkout worker the coupon, which I now realize I probably didn't need to do, and she looked at it a bit then scanned it and I walked away with a free giftcard. At the same time, my roommate went to another self checkout station and got 3 things of orange juice, a couple frozen pizzas, and a bag of Tyson chicken strips for under $5 with no problems.

After Walmart, we decided to head over to Kmart to go for a Subway giftcard. When I brought it up to the register, the cashier looked at it for a moment, was about to call over a manager, then was like fuck it lemme just try to scan it. It wouldn't scan so he gave me the gift card and coupon and told me to go over the customer service area. While walking over, I noticed that the barcodes for the coupon and card didn't match but decided to head over to customer service anyways. Over there, the worker looked at it then went over and took down a paper on the wall with a picture of the $175 off an RCA tv coupon from the hc pack and explained how they don't accept those kinds of coupon. She was pretty smart and noticed that the expiration dates on the two coupons were exactly the same and so were the addresses that it said to send to. I was a little surprised to see that the expiration dates on many of the hc coupons are the same since I know most of the dates on the oc coupons are different. Anyways, I probably won't be going back to that Kmart to use any hc coupons, at least for a while.

After the failure at Kmart I went across the street to CVS and picked up a $20 Dominos giftcard. After the cashier scanned it, the register prompted for manager approval so she just reached around the corner and grabbed a key and approved the coupon and I walked out with the free giftcard.

So, it was a pretty successful run. Saved about $60 in 30 minutes. My only suggestion for you, PL, is that you change up the expiration dates on each HC coupon the next time you update them. If you haven't already bought both coupons packs, DO IT NOW! You're missing out on hundreds of dollars of savings! I plan on trying out the xbox coupon as soon as I get some nice looking paper so I'll update you all on how that goes.

Title: Re: PurpleLotus - Vendor of USA coupons - Newbie Review Thread
Post by: Klipp on February 01, 2013, 07:10 pm
Quote from: AAfive on February 01, 2013, 06:41 pm
I think I am going to have to pull the trigger and try these out!  I have looked at your postings before and wondered how effective they could be, but from all I have read they seem to work most of the time, and that is a HUGE savings.

I look forward to trying them out (or better yet, making my wife do it)

Do it! I've been couponing with PLs coupons for over half a year, and with my own coupon generator for a bit over a month, and I have literally saved THOUSANDS of dollars. I will typically save hundreds _every time_ I go shopping, just because of these coupon offerings.

As for getting your wife to do it, I'd strongly suggest you at least tag along. For one, it's an excellent confidence booster, and helps you understand how to interact under pressure, which I hope will never be a requirement for anyone here, but given that we ARE on the Silk Road, it's quite possible that at some point or another, we will have to be able to communicate effectively while being questioned. Secondly, if you are together, you will likely have a mutual excitement that will grow into having new ideas for coupons that will enrich your lives even further. And finally, couponing with a spouse, significant other or perhaps even children improves your own "trustability" in the eyes of the cashier. It's easy to suspect a single male of intentionally using fake coupons, but it's significantly less easy to suspect a family man ;)

Enjoy the savings, and let me know if you need any help or advice!
Title: Re: PurpleLotus - Vendor of USA coupons - Newbie Review Thread
Post by: Klipp on February 01, 2013, 07:39 pm
I'll also say that if you're still on the fence, just use the current freebie coupon. As of this moment, it's been downloaded over 20 times, after releasing it just ~2 hours ago.

If it's your very first run, I would suggest the following:

1) Print out the freebie coupon on http://couponerpcuhkcyn.onion/ using black and white ink on plain paper
2) Print out 2-3 coupons from coupons.com or smartsource.com (unnecessary, but improves your own confidence and the confidence of the cashier, as well as bolsters your plausible deniability)
3) Go to Target or Walmart (preferably Target, if that's an options) and pick up three boxes of the largest General Mills cereal (20.5oz), in addition to the other items you have coupons for from the other websites. If you're going shopping anyhow, feel free to add whatever other items you need that you would get anyway.
4) When checking out, the cashier will first scan all of your items, I leave my coupons at the end of the products on the conveyor belt. 9 times out of 10, the cashier will just scan the coupons and give you your total. If on the off chance they question where you got the cereal coupon, just say you got it from doing surveys online.
5) Pay with cash.

If you buy the smaller boxes of cereal (so that the total for all 3 is less than 7.50), Target should in fact reduce your total bill by the overage. Walmart will reduce the savings on the coupon to the total cost of the cereal.

That should give you a nice taste, and whet your appetite for more savings!

As you get more confidence, you will be able to walk in with a stack of these coupons and only these coupons, and have no additional items, and not fret even a little bit. The coupons scan just like any other, and several hundred people have been using them successfully for quite a while with not a single mention of anyone getting into even the slightest bit of trouble from them (with regard to PL's offerings and my coupon generator). Eventually, you may progress to using the HardCore coupon pack, where you can get free $25 or $50 gift cards and free or near-free high-end electronic devices.

I hit three WalMarts yesterday, trying to max out the $50 limit for CSM approval each time. I'm finally preferentially picking human cashiers, 2/3 for this outing. And I no longer worry about the coupon exceeding the item price, though I haven't been paid to shop...yet!

One checkout went flawlessly. I picked a female cashier, though she got swapped out for a male just as my I got to the head of the line. I had asked the same guy for help finding something earlier, but I don't think he was a manager.

If memory serves, I think I paid a little over $6 for well over $50 worth of groceries. I definitely remember the cashier comment as he handed me my change, "You made a killing."

I owe it to PL and Klipp, the Assassins of High Prices.
Title: WalMart 2 - should've stayed away from the express checkout
Post by: Abbie Hoffman on February 04, 2013, 02:44 pm
The fist WM cashier experience went well, so I was wanting to use one again. Most lines were backed up w/ a half-dozen customers or more each. I saw the express lane and thought - erroneously, I now realize - that the cashier would be too focused on getting people out the door to pay much notice to my fraudulent coupons. Wrong!

I got more scrutiny of the coupons from her than I ever have at WM. Still, even though she called her Customer Svc Mngr over, neither of them ever looked up at me or even suggested that I was doing anything wrong.

"They all scanned, so I have to take them," is what I overheard her tell the CSM. And I was trying to use the Glad Force Flex on another Glad product. They told me I had to buy the specified quantity-sized product, though they didn't make note of the fact I was trying to use the coupon for recycle bags, rather than Force Flex bags. No problem, I just had them take out the Glad bags and I wound up paying ten bucks and coins for about $50 worth of goods.

Halleluiah!

Title: Re: PurpleLotus - Vendor of USA coupons - Newbie Review Thread
Post by: jackchurchill on February 05, 2013, 01:36 am
I just got back from another Walmart trip.  My brother and I loaded the cart the highest we have tried so far while also attempting to use roughly 10 coupons we had yet to try.  We attempted to try two HC coupons in this trip as well.  We tried to use the xbox 360 controller and the Subway GC coupons.  We made the mistake of telling the sales associate in electronics that we would pay for the xbox controller separate from the rest of the purchase so we wouldn't have to have him accompany us to the front register with the item since we still had shopping to do.  The cashier in his 20's was more than happy to ring up the coupon, unfortunately it was very slow in electronics and his immediate supervisor happened to see the coupon.  My brother and I watched her look over the coupon for a few minutes and then came over and said they couldn't accept a coupon such as this.  I asked her for a further explanation and she was unable to give me one.  Since I had watched what she was doing while looking at the coupon, I could very clearly tell that her rejecting the coupon was solely based on her discretion and nothing else since she hadn't communicated with anyone else or cross-referenced any existing information.  We politely told the manager that we would just email Microsoft regarding the coupon and find an accepting location.  In the future, I am positive that if I were to pay for this item at the front register as opposed to the electronics section this coupon would very easily be passed.  I have noticed that employees who work in the electronics department often take their positions more seriously than traditional cashiers.  In all we had 35 items in our cart with a total of 21 PL coupons.  We paid a total of $6.XX for $126.XX in total goods.  To be honest, the only challenge my brother and I had was making sure we had an actual balance to pay for.  We realized that as we were about to checkout we were close to -$10.00 and decided to throw in non-coupon items into our cart just to make it less of a hassle at the register. 

For overall HC results we are 4/5 on Subway GC's, 1/1 on Keurig Machine and 0/1 on the xbox controller.  I wish we could do more damage on the HC but all of the Walmart's in my area have a very limited GC section and unfortunately the UPC's don't match on some of the few they have.  The OC collection has been essentially perfect to this day.  The only failures were completely on myself/printer errors.  PL is truly an artist and you are simply throwing away money by not using the OC collection at a minimum.   

@PL: Do you know which retailers are best for using the GC's?  We found a target in the area but didn't fully understand their coupon policy and since I am currently broke, I didn't want to risk using my limited funds and not maximizing my grocery supply.  Any help would be greatly appreciated and thanks again for keeping our panty full.

Title: Re: PurpleLotus - Vendor of USA coupons - Newbie Review Thread
Post by: purplelotus on February 05, 2013, 04:14 pm
Quote from: jackchurchill on February 05, 2013, 01:36 am
@PL: Do you know which retailers are best for using the GC's?  We found a target in the area but didn't fully understand their coupon policy and since I am currently broke, I didn't want to risk using my limited funds and not maximizing my grocery supply.  Any help would be greatly appreciated and thanks again for keeping our panty full.

Walgreens seems to be awesome with the GCs. I would avoid trying to use a coupon over $50 at Target, because it seems to work in some areas while not working in others, but anything $50 and under seems to have no issues. Also, there is one major flaw in what you said... don't ever pay full price for anything, bud. If your coupon is ever rejected, just tell them you changed your mind and don't want the product anymore and to take it off. This is the way real couponers act, so it certainly doesn't do anything to add to any suspicion.

PL

Title: Re: PurpleLotus - Vendor of USA coupons - Newbie Review Thread
Post by: purplelotus on February 05, 2013, 06:52 pm
Regretfully, I have been informed that Klipp will be resigning from the coupon game in order to pursue better opportunities in life. This will also mean we are collectively retiring the .onion coupon generator. I left the choice up to Klipp and he decided it was in the best interest of his personal safety not to let me take his work and continue with it on my own. I wish this was not the case, but I certainly hold no hard feelings towards him and neither should anyone else. I respect his decision and wish him the best of luck in his future endeavors.

The credit listings are now down, but now I have to address the issue of those of you with remaining credits. Klipp has agreed to allow the site to stay live until Friday evening, in which time you will be free to use any many credits as you have left between now and then. Anyone who has credits left that they paid for on Friday evening, will be given a full refund for those remaining credits. If you want to request the refund now, that is fine too. I wish this wasn't the case and I certainly apologize to anyone who this inconveniences. Klipp has been gracious enough to return to me enough money to cover his side of the refunds in advance, and depending on whether people burn up their credits or ask for refunds, Klipp has already handed over the money back to me to cover him and I must admit that shows a lot of class.

This is disappointing news, of course, but one thing I promise is that I am not slowing down anytime soon. Goodbye Klipp, and again good luck! Even though we didn't really make any money together, we had a fun time not doing it. :-)

PL

Title: Re: PurpleLotus - Vendor of USA coupons - Newbie Review Thread
Post by: purplelotus on February 05, 2013, 07:47 pm
Quote from: jacklinks on February 05, 2013, 06:59 pm
One question I have: I have noticed that some of the cards do not have a UPC. They simply have a barcode and the gift card number. Do the coupons ever work on a gift card like this?

When you find the GCs with the long sequence of numbers and seemingly no UPC (this happens, but not terribly often, at least to me)... see if you can find the first 5 digits of the UPC in that sequence of numbers. for example, if the first 5 are "99366" and you can find the exact same sequence somewhere in that string of numbers, then you have yourself the correct card. Sometimes you may have to peel a strip back a bit to see those numbers (mainly on some VISA cards). then I simply grab a different card and put the one I pulled back a little back and go checkout.

PL

@asmat3000: Read your coupon policies for each store. Like for Target the max of the same identical coupon you can use is 4, but also be aware that the machine does not make this decision on it's own, only the cashier can catch it. So there's that..

Title: Re: PurpleLotus - Vendor of USA coupons - Newbie Review Thread
Post by: FugNuggetz on February 07, 2013, 03:23 pm
PL's coupons are exactly as advertised. All the ones I have tried work, and the hardcore ones are literally an entirely separate item that is labeled hardcore for a reason.

In regards to the coupon's themselves:

The scannable portion of the coupone (barcode) is generated based on an algorithm. The numbers contain the corresponding item or brand and also the amount to be discounted. Unless the store has a programmed LIMIT % price change, STOP, or  GET MANAGER value on the price changing function for a particular item/brand (or as an overall store policy) then any scanner should accept the barcode on the coupon and perform the discount operation. CHECK THE BARCODE on the product before you go to use a coupon, make sure it corresponds and you will have a much higher success rate.

Every store has different coupon policies, employees, and managers. Your success is much more dependent on your ability to assess these three variables and make intelligent decisions regarding the situation, rather than on the coupon's validity itself. The coupon will always scan if it corresponds to the barcode on the item. If use of a coupon becomes widespread enough there is likely a corporate notice to store managers about said coupon, which would then probably be entered into aforementioned scanning system and would then return a fail to scan or get manager output. Coupons for higher valued items are obviously more likely to be scrutinized and return get manager messages. 

Also, as an addendum, using the same coupons over a long period of time will likely not work because the store will find out they are fake whenever they are not reimbursed by the manufacturer  (based on however frequently they send in their coupons for reimbursement.)


That being said PL's coupons are awesome when used correctly and he has been helpful and hasty in every aspect. I can't see how anyone could complain about his coupons, if you can't use them in such a way that you at least break even on the price of them with your savings then it is likely a user error if you get my drift.

TL;DR The coupons are fine, find a store with a dumb staff and make sure to match the item barcode to the coupon. Have a good explanation or plan of action ready in case you are confronted. Do these things and success will follow.

The next coupon was $2.75 off of a $2.98 product. It scanned but this screen popped up and said to hold the coupon and show it to the cashier (CSR). I put it in the slot anyway, hit ok and it took me back to the scanning screen. I scanned the next one. It was for $7 off of Cottonelle but the actual cost was $6.98. I got the screen to show it to the cashier and had already put it in the slot but here she was and she over rode it because it did not take 7 bucks off the total.  I'm sure she saw that I was supposed to call her for the previous one but didn't and that's why she came over.

I had the last coupon in my hand which was for $9.75 off of  $11 as well and she said, "lets try this one." I had a feeling in my gut that going to the service desk would cause problems so I just gave up.

Title: Re: PurpleLotus - Vendor of USA coupons - Newbie Review Thread
Post by: jackchurchill on February 10, 2013, 05:52 am
@ xxqvxx

I personally stopped using the self-checkout after a my first couple tries between Walmart and a regional store.  My items eventually worked both times but it was a considerable hassle compared to the relative ease I have had speaking with a real cashier.  Most of the cashiers I have dealt with have no interest in speaking with their managers unless the machine forces them to have a csm turn the key.  The csm usually goes to the register, ignores you completely and then turn the key as quick as they can and leave to go do real work.  I believe that the issues regarding self-checkout stem from the stores already focusing on everyday theft that occurs regularly at these self-checkout stands.  Plenty of people not involved with PL already try to sneak one over on Walmart by not scanning all of their items, bar-code changing or simply using a coupon that matches UPC's but don't qualify based on the stipulations of use.  Walmart assumes that they don't need to have a csm approve these in the same way with a cashier because one of their trained cashiers should already be preventing this from happening. 

When I first started, I began with just a few coupons that I used and built up how many I used as I was able to confirm personal success with each coupon.  I feel by going with this method, you allow yourself never to feel flustered by having multiple scanning issues in the same trip.  I started with just a few, and last time I used 21 coupons with complete success.  It sounds like you have a great idea for being able to help others while also helping yourself which is great.  That is what this scene is all about from what I have noticed.  I know it was a great feeling being able to help a friend stock his fridge a few times and also get his gf an awesome birthday present while during lean times.   Good luck on your next run and hope you soon see the success most of us see every trip soon!

From what I've read and experienced in nearly $1,000 worth of personal savings w/ PL products, maybe 1%-10% cashiers will balk at the OC - but more often than not, they'll be overruled by the CSM, who will approve them.

And never ever have the OC - or the few HC that I've used, for that matter - ever resulted in me being followed back to my car by Loss Prevention or caused me to get any obvious scrutiny. And Loss Prevention is VERY obvious in most cases, to anyone with even basic observational skills.

To the contrary, using the OC and a human cashier makes you look MORE like a legitimate customer than the average shopper - seriously, it truly does. Dressing well, acting politely, shopping when they're busy AND being an innocent-looking couponer will help you avoid LP more than whether or not you use the OC.

Quote from: 420blindman
...Found some info that can help when possibly being questioned about any coupons, not just PLs. The biggest lawsuit brought to big box stores is slander (accusing you of using fraudulent coupons), and unlawful detention (holding you against your will, and with zero authority). Both of these usually end in a payout to the victim, in order to avoid court.
From my personal experience, when being questioned, it's normally nothing, and I'll just ask not to use the one coupon that's causing the trouble. However, when they have an attitude or are being snotty, then I'll raise my voice pretty loud and demand if the are accusing me of a crime. I make a scene, and demand to see management. Title: Local chains
Post by: Abbie Hoffman on February 20, 2013, 05:51 am
The standard advice is to stick w/ the big three - WM, Target & The K - but what is surprising are the regional and smaller chains where PL's coups DO work. I'm in the middle of nowhere, so having a couple of local chains where I can use PL's work saves a lot on gas. I've picked up a couple of Wendy's gc's at one and the other apparently has a policy of hiring only hotties for cashiers. Schwing!

I'm still feeling out that place (and enjoying it like a dirty old man should enjoy his grocery shopping), but it doesn't look like getting a manager to turn the key there is at all hard. It's just as easy as WM, the K or most other places. (And some of their managers seem to be teen hotties too!)

Only one local chain has outright refused to take the coupons at all. And for all I know, that was just one rouge cashier. Regardless, no big loss since that's the chain w/ the shittiest selection. At another the manager held up the checkout line for the better part of 10 minutes, smiling and shaking his head while he stared at the coups. In the end, though, he accepted them all.
And another location/manager/time of day could produce much more favorable conditions.

Title: Re: PurpleLotus - Vendor of USA coupons - Newbie Review Thread
Post by: TwoneNathandjoe on February 26, 2013, 04:16 am
California, you can easily make an argument in either direction, but from over here the larger organizations, especially wal-mart, are victimizing the commuinities they are "feeding". Consider firstly that Wal-Mart has a higher profit yearly than many countries, AFTER they pay their employees and other costs, and yet still don't pay their part-time employees any health benefits, not to mention that many people, even after working at wal-mart for many years STILL make incredibly small wages, usually no more than $12 per hour after 5-10 years. The health package for full-time associates has declined over the years to almost nothing. They've phased out full-time employees that aren't management to almost nothing, to avoid paying health care. They selectively weed out employees reaching full-vestment time in order prevent paying their promised share of retirement.

Wal-Mart uses predatory methods to pay the lowest amount possible for their wholesale products, at times leaching companies providing products literally to death and then moving on to another source to bleed. On the other end of this same method, local stores which would pay employees fairly are choked out of communities.

I won't deny that this is theft, legally speaking, I just have a hard time giving a good goddamn.

California, you can easily make an argument in either direction, but from over here the larger organizations, especially wal-mart, are victimizing the commuinities they are "feeding". Consider firstly that Wal-Mart has a higher profit yearly than many countries, AFTER they pay their employees and other costs, and yet still don't pay their part-time employees any health benefits, not to mention that many people, even after working at wal-mart for many years STILL make incredibly small wages, usually no more than $12 per hour after 5-10 years. The health package for full-time associates has declined over the years to almost nothing. They've phased out full-time employees that aren't management to almost nothing, to avoid paying health care. They selectively weed out employees reaching full-vestment time in order prevent paying their promised share of retirement.

Wal-Mart uses predatory methods to pay the lowest amount possible for their wholesale products, at times leaching companies providing products literally to death and then moving on to another source to bleed. On the other end of this same method, local stores which would pay employees fairly are choked out of communities.

I won't deny that this is theft, legally speaking, I just have a hard time giving a good goddamn.

Title: Re: PurpleLotus - Vendor of USA coupons - Newbie Review Thread
Post by: Abbie Hoffman on February 26, 2013, 06:21 pm
Regarding WalMart, $50 worth of coupons is the cut-off for requiring CSM approval. I'm not sure if that's $50 and above or just above $50, but if you keep the coupon total under $50 you just have to get past the cashier.

And if you go right after the suppertime rush, maybe around 6-7 PM, you have a better chance of a cashier not caring enough to second-glance the coupons.

HTH
Title: Re: PurpleLotus - Vendor of USA coupons - Newbie Review Thread
Post by: Abbie Hoffman on February 26, 2013, 06:38 pm
I think that's true about about the coupon exceeding the item price producing a Point-Of-Sale warning message/beep. But, most of the cashiers are just going to click right through that error, as long as you've got an item from the right manufacturer.

I should say that does suck about the suspicious cashier and manager. I've had a hiccup or two in a couple of months of passing over $1500 worth of coupons. But, I think if you try a new WalMart this weekend - or better several WalMarts, KMarts and Targets - keeping the coupon value under $50 per WalMart checkout, you will have much better luck. And Target seems much friendlier.

You and your wife probably looked fine and would have sailed through checkout, if not for the asshole cashier and manager, and maybe the time of day you shopped. Try, try again...

Title: Re: PurpleLotus - Vendor of USA coupons - Newbie Review Thread
Post by: jacob1234 on February 27, 2013, 07:16 pm
Quote from: bucklemyshoe1 on February 27, 2013, 04:13 pm
how do you print the coupon without it being a full page wide ? or is it supposed to be that big?

What I do for the OC coupons is open a word processor, make it where I can see the layout (the print area), drag and drop the coupon in and resize to fit in the print region. Can usually fit three horizontal coupons as well as two vertical ones with a horizontal below those.

Hope that helps.

I just opened them with the default windows picture viewer, pressed print and unchecked the fit to screen option -- worked perfectly for all of mine.

Title: Re: PurpleLotus - Vendor of USA coupons - Newbie Review Thread
Post by: Abbie Hoffman on February 28, 2013, 07:30 am
Quote from: LSB16 on February 28, 2013, 06:54 am
Has anyone had any luck with the Chick-fil-a coupon? Was gonna go get lunch tomorrow and don't want to look like an asshole =o)

No, but TRY IT. Worst case, the manager is an asshole and you try somewhere else. I got rebuffed at the only Chick-fil-a I tried, then went by McD's and drove away w/ a free supersized Big Mac, Fries & Coke. And the coupon says "for the greater Los Angelas area only." It just takes a little bit of calm confidence & social engineering. But you'll be surprised how easy it is.

Go during lunch or dinner rush hour, preferably toward the end of it, but not long enough for them to put their second string in. And I'm guessing that, like retail couponing, your best bet is on the weekend, when the experienced folks are off work and the crowds overwhelm the cashiers. Dress well and act reasonably nice.

Title: Re: PurpleLotus - Vendor of USA coupons - Newbie Review Thread
Post by: jacob1234 on March 01, 2013, 07:28 am
Quote from: powerndknowledge on March 01, 2013, 04:55 am
my question is if i have two general mills coupons same ones and two boxes would it stack? also why are some coupons not working even if the bar code and upc code are same? thanks !

Okay. Well I hope I can help with the first part. To answer your question about stacking... it just depends on your store policy. I know the same question came up on the regular forums about this, and PL said at Target he'd stacked more than store policy because the computers don't stop it. So just check into the policy of the store. And if you can't find it that way just try it. The worst they can say is no and you can put the second item aside.

As for the other problem, all coupons (legit or counterfeit) have their problems. Sometimes it's the store, but sometimes they just don't scan right. I'd make sure they're trying both barcodes if there's some kind of error coming up. Because I know (at least for one local chain here) they HAVE to scan the UPC barcode or it messes up every time. If the gs1 is scanned it sends the computer an error, so they usually cover it up so the UPC barcode is scanned.

I'll report back and see if I have any problems with those specific coupons though.

using that paper will require a laser printer or possibly an epson printer with dura-ink. I know epson can print on teslin paper which requires a laser printer so thats a guess.  I found a few sites selling 32# laser gloss paper etc


Paper Options:

There are many different paper grades, weights and brands on the market from a variety of mills. Publishers select the type of paper that not only meets their customers' requirements, but also works well in their machinery.

Weight
Paper is categorized by weight in pounds of a ream (500 sheets) of paper cut to a standard size, 25" x 38" for text paper, 20" x 26" for cover weight papers. For example - 500 sheets 25" x 38" of 70# coated paper will weigh 70 pounds.
Weight has not only an effect on the feel of the magazine (heavier paper will generally be thicker and less easy to fold) but also shipping/mailing costs of the final magazine. More weight costs more to ship/mail.

Grade Specifications
A grade is a way of ranking paper by certain composition and characteristics. For example, brightness is one of the characteristics used to determine a paper's grade. A number 5 paper grade has the lowest brightness (less white and uniform texture), from 69-73. A number 3 grade paper has a brightness from 81-84.5. Number 1 grade paper has 89-96 brightness. Most magazines run on #3-#5 grade stock.

Uncoated Offset Paper
Uncoated Paper is designed to generally run in offset presses and is a non-coated sheet of #50 or 60#. Also- return card offset stock is usually run on a 75# uncoated stock to meet postal requirements.

Freesheet Paper
Freesheet paper is free of groundwood pulp and has a bit higher brightness (whiter) than groundwood paper. Freesheet starts at a number 3 grade. Magazines commonly use 50#, 60#, 70# text weight freesheet options on the interior and 80#, 100# text weight or 66# cover weight freesheet stock on cover options. Freesheet paper is more costly than Groundwood.

Groundwood Paper
Characteristics of groundwood paper are higher bulk, smooth feel, lower brightness (whiteness) and good printability. It is usually lower in cost than freesheet paper. Magazines commonly use 36#, 40#, 45#, 50# and 60# groundwood paper. Groundwood is available in number 4 or number 5 grade.

Coated Offset Paper
Coated papers are described by their finish: matte, dull, or gloss.

    Gloss- The majority of magazines today use gloss paper, the property responsible for coated paper's shiny or lustrous appearance. Gloss papers are less opaque and have less bulk and are less expensive than Dull and Matte papers.

    Dull- Smooth surface paper that is low in gloss. Dull coated paper falls between matte and glossy paper.

    Matte- A non-glossy, flat looking paper. Matte papers are higher in cost and in bulk.

Title: Re: PurpleLotus - Vendor of USA coupons - Newbie Review Thread
Post by: The_Real_Batman on March 03, 2013, 02:22 am
I feel like I should give some feed back here, since I've used the original and hardcore coupons a bit. So far only managed to get the xbox live to work from the hardcore set. Here's my input thus far:

Xbox live worked at target. Had to go to three different cashiers until finally getting a assistant manager to approve the transaction. The first two were regular associates so were unable to approve it. For the newbies, most stores have a cut off between $40-50 dollars before needed manager, or assistant manager approval in order to accept coupons. In the forums you will see people refer to this as a "key turn", since the manager technically turns a key in the register to override the computer system put in place.

With any run, you will be surprised what you get away with. At target for the Xbox Live Card, a police officer, and two security guards were both standing and sitting leisurely behind the manager while placing my transaction. No fucks were given by either parties. Now this was late before closing, and they could have just not given a fuck. I know I didn't to be honest. It was a long day. Remember all they can do is say no. If they question you, simple speak out your ass about getting them off a survey, having a family member that's a hard core couponer, etc. You'd be surprised the bullshit that will come out your mouth.

In my experience the original coupons are a no brainer.  So long as you stick to a large grocery store franchise, or you get lucky at one of those smaller local places. For smaller places, I would ask, or go for a test run before going all out and filling up my cart. Many people continue success with Target, Walmart, and other major grocery stores. Hell I even had a cashier check "the book" in order to validate the legitimacy of the original coupons. Came back and I ask her if there was a problem. In which she replied, "I just had to check our book to make sure the coupons were not fraudulent." Had to contain my laughter. Felt on top of the world getting away with that. And had even more respect for PurpleLotus with his immaculate work.

I try my best to not hit the same store more then once, or twice a month. Some people get away with once a week. I wouldn't doubt it, just switch up your times so as you don't run into the same staff during their shifts. And if you did hit a store once a week, make it a big store like walmart or something. PurpleLotus once mentioned, when a manager tries to tell you some bullshit, take it with a grain of salt. Example: I went to one Walgreens which the manager claimed, they didn't take cigarette coupons. Which of course was bullshit because I just finished hitting up another Walgreens with success. So feed them the same bullshit right back.

It's always good to read store coupon policies as well. Trust me, if you do, you'll be ahead of the game. Let's face it, no employees ever have to read that shit. Even if they did, they would probably read over it the same way you read over terms of service of anything you sign up for. Which you don't. Point being. I believe appearance also plays a factor. Don't look like a bum. It will come off suspicious. Be curious, and respectful. Your goal is for them to scan your coupon and see if it goes through. If they don't want to accept it, try and at least convince them to scan it. So you yourself knows it works on said product, with said barcode. If it does, well shit congrats. If not, well fuck, just say, "thank you for trying, I'll go to dumbfuckville and try there." But remember that product, so you know what to look for.

Quote
PurpleLotus has said it time and time again, all they can say is no.

Simple. If they try and say, oh these look fake or whatever else to deny your legitimacy, just laugh it off as a compliment. Say, yeah I get that often. Coupons are not easy to come by, but most people don't take the time to take simple surveys. Sometimes I go as far as feeding them so much bullshit, that even I begin to believe my own bullshit, but that's what you want.

Once you walk into a store, know you're a motherfucking god of couponing. You know the system, this isn't your first time. You save shit loads every week. You spend hours cutting out coupons for magazines, and taking online surveys, and you also print internet coupons out for being a member of online coupon websites. Don't let them feed you the bullshit that there's not such thing as printed coupons. They just don't know there way around the internet. Internet coupons have been around for years. Hmm can't add on to anything else. I hope this helps though.

By the way, when you print your coupons, color or black and white, make sure they are in good enough shape to scan. Don't print them out to small, or to large. You want them to look like real coupons, and most importantly you want them to scan. Yes I did go to a store once, and had the cashier type in manually like 10 coupons. Felt like that was a bit of amateur mistake on my part. Buy a printer, buy ink, and save yourself the trouble. Plus going to a print shop adds up. Pro tip: Get a HP Printer. You'll have a ten dollar off HP ink coupon.

Cheers.

If you check the UPC of the coupon the 7th to 9th number "5 xxxxx000xx 0" if it has 3 0s that means anything in that family will ring up.  example $2 off lunchables.  well walmart has them for $1.25 (cheap ones) but the coupon says for BOXED well if you pick up the cheap ones you make .75 for each coupon because it will take $2 off instead of just the value for the lunchable.  This is actually legit couponing and many "traditional" couponers did it.

So I've learned the HC coupons are really not that easy to pass off. The past three weeks, I haven't had much luck on any of them. I also think Walgreens knows what's up, since every time I try to redeem a gift card, they're just not having it. I spoke to one Assistant manager, and he said that there was an email sent out to all the supervisors in which stated to be careful of fraudulent coupons. Stating that if it's to good to be true, it probably is. Maybe I just fucked over one to many walgreens, who know. CVS seems to be the same as well. It's disappointing since it really was sort of like a candy store for gift cards. I mean they carry like all of them.

I tried a K-mart today with the Food Saver Vacuum coupon. This was actually the second time I tried it. It was denied both at Target, and K-mart. Just didn't ring up right. Supposedly K-mart is cracking down on coupons as well. I'm going to try walmart tomorrow, since most people have had the best luck there. So far the OC coupons haven't failed though. Only thing is I can't seem to find the HP ink product UPCs to match the coupon. Sucks, since I really need some black ink. It's amazing how fast you blow through ink using these coupons. Worth it.

To add, if you want a smoother transaction, profile the cashiers. I do my best to stray away from the older Cashiers, as they tend to take there job way to seriously. The younger ones really don't give a fuck. Hell they'll barely even look at the coupon. I swear the older ones analyze each and every one of them though. No one has time for that shit. It's just frustrating standing there with my thumb up my ass. Who cares though right, it's all about the savings.

Hmm can't really add anything else to this. Just always make sure you have enough cash on you. Don't be afraid to ask questions even if a coupon is denied. I feel like I learn a lot from managers, associates, etc when questioning why a coupon hasn't gone through.

Also never be discouraged. It can be easy to be once denied time and time again (for those of you on the Hardcore Coupons) Just remember it's a hustle.  With rejection comes acceptance, experience, knowledge, and confidence. Don't give up, just push harder. It's not easy to fuck over the system, but there's always a way.

Title: Re: PurpleLotus - Vendor of USA coupons - Newbie Review Thread
Post by: WaterWorks on March 05, 2013, 02:04 pm
Quote from: wraithe on March 05, 2013, 03:43 am
If you check the UPC of the coupon the 7th to 9th number "5 xxxxx000xx 0" if it has 3 0s that means anything in that family will ring up.  example $2 off lunchables.  well walmart has them for $1.25 (cheap ones) but the coupon says for BOXED well if you pick up the cheap ones you make .75 for each coupon because it will take $2 off instead of just the value for the lunchable.  This is actually legit couponing and many "traditional" couponers did it.

Thanks for the tip!

Title: Re: PurpleLotus - Vendor of USA coupons - Newbie Review Thread
Post by: Abbie Hoffman on March 05, 2013, 06:15 pm
Quote from: WaterWorks on March 05, 2013, 02:15 pm
Has anyone tried the OC at Publix?

The standard advice is "stick to the big three (WM, Target & K-Mart)", but I've had some success with regional stores, as well as CVS, Rite-Aid and Walgreens, so I'd be tempted to try a couple under-$5's at a Publix, if the nearest one wasn't 100 miles from here.

Anybody have real world experience w/ Publix? Their employees are supposed to be treated better than most other stores, so they might be concerned and even intelligent enough to be suspicious. But their customer service is so well-renowned that they might let a small number of small-dollar coups slide.

The worst that you would likely get is a polite refusal.

HTH

Has anyone tried the OC at Publix?

Items sometimes are a bit more there, but look out for their buy one get one free items. You can mix in a coupon with that, and save big. I do this with there Orange Juice and Cereals.

Title: Re: PurpleLotus - Vendor of USA coupons - Newbie Review Thread
Post by: wraithe on March 06, 2013, 05:20 pm
Quote from: 2L5D on March 06, 2013, 04:58 pm
thx for all the helpful replies! learned a lot just reading this thread.

Can anyone answer this for me...

Have you gone and done a shopping trip, buying 20+ items, with those items being only for what you've coupons for?
Good idea, bad idea, or null?

Can you do it...yes
Should you do it.... occasionally is ok

The last thing you want to do is draw attention to yourself.  Many members here have taken $800 in coupons and walked out paying a few bucks.  Why draw attention to yourself I ask?  Doing things of that nature imprint your experience into employees heads.  Thats the guy that got 100boxes of trojan condoms for $1.50.

It is my opinion there are only two things that will ruin your experience and possible involve le.  Greed and Stupidity.

examples of greed. $800 of stuff paying $1 lol, hitting the same store over and over and over., using one HC coupon at say the electronics counter then going to regular checkout with some more HC coupons( I have done this, I do not recommend it lol), etc

examples of stupidity.  Selling coupon'd shit on ebay, posting pictures of your shit and not removing meta-tags, bragging about your couponing on public forums.  Hitting the same store over and over(that one falls into both categories because not only is it greedy, its also stupid lol)

If you have an idea on how to use a coupon, ask yourself if its an example of greed or stupidity, if not your greenlit to go lol.

**edited** I also aim for quantity over quality.  I would rather hit a walmart for $50 a trip for the next 12 months(feasible with the oc coupon updates) and never draw attention to myself and no one be the wise, then hitting them hard for $300 in one sitting and then drawing attention.  Slow and steady wins the race the turtle said.  With updated offer codes and coupon reworking, there is no way they would know your passing a fake coupon.  No way to prove it other then calling the manufacturer, other then using common sense i.e. $250 off Beats by Dre is absurd and only idiots believe its real lol.  No one is ever going to question your $2 off coupon for lunchables.

I agree with you 100%. last thing I want is for any CSM to be called over. sure it's just a key turn, but that just opens a door to be questioned. my wife and I now have a great system where we get just under the $50 saving limit at Walmart (at 50 you need CSM override) and we do our shopping. we will each take a separate check out lane and separate our groceries into two separate transactions. By doing this the cashier can just do her job (they dont care they are just there to scan shit) and we never need  CSM to come by and see out ridiculous savings. The best part is by splitting it up we still save up to $200 on one visit to the store and we make out like ninjas in the night and no one is the wiser. Stealth. so to clarify my wife will do two separate transactions, while i am in a different lane also doing two separate transactions all while we are keeping below the $50 savings limit per transaction to maintain stealth.

Title: Re: PurpleLotus - Vendor of USA coupons - Newbie Review Thread
Post by: The_Real_Batman on March 13, 2013, 06:57 am
Quote from: kpnitreal1 on March 13, 2013, 04:37 am
How does this work exactly?

Simple. Skim through the thread a bit towards the beginning. Now you're also going to want to go ahead and check out the Main Thread as well. Maybe pages 1-10 or so. Though I most definitely encourage you to read a lot more. Everyone here, and there started exactly were you are at. After that, you can get started printing your coupons and saving money. One thing you should know is to not print all 200+ coupons at once. Do one first. If the coupon size and quality look good, now is the time you take to skim through which coupons you find of interest. You print those only. Make sure you check the dates on them as well.

Most importantly, PAY WITH CASH!! You don't ever want to pay with a credit/debit card. Remember you don't want a paper trail.

If any problem shall arise, just ask here in the forums, but you have to be a lot more specific then; "So how's this work?"

Luckily I'm so not low (High) at the moment, feeling nice, and a bit spunky (don't ask). So there you go.

Cheers mate.

Ninja Edit: Holy shit I had a shit load of typos. Sorry about that. I was just pretty high last night. Fun times.

Let me start off by saying that PurpleLotus is a total bastard, and my life is now ruined because of him...

HOW THE HELL AM I SUPPOSED TO PAY FULL RETAIL FOR ANYTHING EVER AGAIN?!

:D :D :D

Seriously, this has been one hell of a week. So crazy. I... I just... FUCK, guys. FUCK.

Can't find the receipt at the moment, but my most recent trip to wal-mart ended with a shopping cart literally overflowing with stuff. After a few test runs I decided to go balls-out and see just what I could do with these things. I wasn't even keeping close track of the total with or without coupons, so I must say there was a lot of anxiety coursing through me as I approached the checkout lane with a fat stack of coupons and about $40 in my pocket. I was prepared to leave as non-chalantly as possible if things went south, but it seems that my worry was for naught...

I bantered with the cashier about the weather as she rang up my stuff, and holy shit was it hard to stay cool as I saw the total creep above $350 after tax. I then very politely handed her a stack of b&w's that weren't even cut out very neatly and apologized for being "an extreme couponer," which she assured me was perfectly fine. Being a newer walmart that isn't busy yet, and the middle of a Thursday, I had no line behind me. I  even joked with her about how "last time an old lady waiting in line got really nasty with me about the delay," and she replied, "God! Some people are so rude!" <3

She kept getting a bit more amazed each time the total slid downward, until I found myself with a cart so full I had bags tied to the handle (!) and a grand total after taxes of... wait...

Motherfuckin' wait for it...



NINETY-TWO CENTS. :o :o :o [craps self with joy]

I actually raised my fists into the air and shouted, "Whoo-hoo!" LMAO The CSM that came for the over-$50-key-turn said, "That's some good shopping, sir." SO hard not to lose my shit right then and there. My. Fucking. God.

That brings the total to probably close to a grand "saved" for the week. I put it in quotations because I think I would have normally spent about as much $ total, but now I have TEN TIMES AS MUCH STUFF. So many toiletries, so much food. I've given away and eaten insane amounts and there's so... much... more.  Ridiculous, stupendous, incredible, beyond description, life-changing, paradigm-shifting-to-the-next-dimension, I-have-no-more-superlatives-left-here-goddamn.

And this is just using the OC collection a few times at a few stores. Haven't even really delved into the HC yet...

Title: Re: PurpleLotus - Vendor of USA coupons - Newbie Review Thread
Post by: purplelotus on March 16, 2013, 03:42 pm
Quote from: bobloblaw on March 16, 2013, 12:19 am
So... I'm honestly kinda confused about how these work! If your purchase the coupons, is it for online purchases only? Or do your customers print them off themselves with a regular printer? Just wondering about logistics haha :)

You just print them off with a regular printer like any other coupon you get off the internet. They look like real internet coupons you would be sent in an e-mail or download off facebook or a website. I could go on and on about it, but these are for IN STORE use only, and do not work online. You print them, walk into the store, let the cashier scan the items, then hand over your coupons when she tells you your total and watch as she begins to scan your coupons, causing your total to drop dramatically.

Title: Re: PurpleLotus - Vendor of USA coupons - Newbie Review Thread
Post by: NotAnAgent on March 25, 2013, 10:34 pm
Well I think it is time to share my experience with the OG collection from PurpleLotus. On Sunday morning, I went to a ghetto Walmart with a stack of PurpleLotus coupons and legit coupons. I used regular inkjet printer paper on "Best" and color.

The first part was finding all the items scattered around the store and matching up the UPC. Unfortunately, there was only one register open and an older Hispanic employee manning the station. I made sure to let a colored lady go first so she didn't have to wait for a long time as I was greedy with a lot of merchandise.

After the total came to $119, abuelito started scanning the coupons and after a few coupons, another old Hispanic female employee approached the register.  :'( They were speaking in Spanish about the coupons being a high amount such as $8 off Bounty and $10 off FoodSaver products. Similar words! As soon as the register locked up, the female employee went to call "Superviso". Ten minutes later, another Hispanic lesbian employee who I assume was the supervisor came and used her magic key twice without even glancing at me and left.  ;D
I believe this occurred because I used over $40 in coupons.

The last employee was a mid 20s Indian "Associate Manager" who scrutinized the shit out of the coupons and told me they don't take Internet coupons. I raised my usually soft spoken voice slightly and told him their coupon policy says otherwise and asked the two other employees for their knowledge on the policy. They shrugged their shoulders and did not know.  ::)

Basically, he let the ones that were already scanned go through but would not scan anymore. I took a few products out and he voided the items. Paid only $36! Walked out with a cart full of groceries and smiled as soon as I reached my vehicle and made sure that no loss prevention was following me.

tl;dr - $119 down to $36. TRY to start off small, check the store's coupon policy and match up the UPC and you're good to go! Already paid for itself as well in one shopping trip.

Itching to use these at dozens of stores here and curious about using them at self-checkouts. Be sure to not use your store 'savings' card or credit card linked to your real name/address. Just open up a new one if you do get savings with different info. Keep the stories coming please!

Title: Re: PurpleLotus - Vendor of USA coupons - Newbie Review Thread
Post by: Abbie Hoffman on March 27, 2013, 03:27 pm
I've heard that the VISA cards expire w/in 24 hrs, but I've also heard that they can take a day to initially be activated. Bottom line, every other gift card I've had or heard of has had zero problems after you leave the store.

Buy some glossy paper, adjust your printer settings, pick up a Shell card from CVS, RiteAid, etc every week or so and you may never buy gas again.  ;D

Title: Re: PurpleLotus - Vendor of USA coupons - Newbie Review Thread
Post by: b00ked1time on April 02, 2013, 08:27 am
Just bought a near free VISA gift card at CVS, feeling like a boss!

To anyone looking how to use the VISA coupons start small and use the $20 off the $25 dollar VISA card, because the cashiers don't need manager approval to accept coupons under $30 (At least at the CVS's in my area). Also from my experience hit drug stores for gift cards, not Target, Walmart, and K-Mart.        CVS is by far the best, then Walgreens, and lastly RiteAid.

Thank you PurpleLotus for the amazing coupons!

Whatever you may think about Chick-Fil-A, I have to give at least one of their managers an A+ for customer service, as well as looking out for her employer's bottom line. After her well-trained and intelligent cashier noticed that my (fraudulent) coupon was for a regular combo, not the grilled chicken I ordered, the manager politely informed me that the coupon was part of an Internet scam.

And then she STILL GAVE ME THE FREE COMBO, saying that she didn't want to penalize me for getting caught up in a scam! +1 Karma!

Anyway, I hope that they catch whoever is scamming poor Chick-Fil-A on the Internet...as long as the free grub (and other consumer goods) keeps coming my way.  ;)

Title: Re: PurpleLotus - Vendor of USA coupons - Newbie Review Thread
Post by: JohnJohnerson333 on April 03, 2013, 02:23 pm
I don't post much, but I wanted to drop by and show my support for PL. 

Mostly all of us are aware that you can find resources out there on how to make your own coupons, free of charge.  But to me, the one time fee you pay for PL's coupon packs are WELL worth the money.  Not only do you get a very solid and already put together list, he also updates them regularly.  I personally am too busy to make 200+ coupons every couple of months, and am beyond thankful that PL provides this service, and would consider it a steal at thrice the price   It is certainly the best money I have spent on the Road, and in the top 5 of the best money I have spent all time.  I have not only stocked a full house of items, but give plenty to friends, family, charities, and people I know who are living on the edge, barely making ends meet.  I even have friends who are educators, who offer their services free of charge to under privileged children in other countries.  Every time they go, or have a fund raiser, or w/e, I always send them with a massive care package to help these people get items that they don't even have access to, little lone the kind of access we have using these coupons.  I'm actually sending a package this week, with a friend who is going to be teaching school as a volunteer for the next month.   

I hope this gets rectified and PL is exonerated and exulted  as the extremely good and helpful person that he is.  Regardless, I am very thankful for the service that PL has provided, and I for one, can verify that the under-privileged world, is a little better off because of this service.
